  69. First off, I will say that this company's customer service was as advertised and I'll give them 2 stars just for that. Beyond that though, I'm not sure what to say. The oil I received had a light greenish/gray tint to it which tells me it was NOT rosehip seed oil. It actually appeared clear in the dropper, but when put in a small, white prescription lid you could see the actual color. From everything I've learned about rosehip seed oil it should have a warm amber or tangerine color to it. There may be variations of the depth of color from batch to batch, but all organic, cold-pressed, rosehip seed oil should have this same characteristic color. If it doesn't, then its either not rosehip seed oil, or its been chemically altered or otherwise processed to remove the color, and would indicate it is not cold-pressed. It should also have a smell to it, described as earthy, tea like or even a faint fishy smell. This oil has no smell whatsoever. For those rave reviews that state this is wonderful facial oil, I can only wonder if these people 1) Are real users of this oil; 2) Are familiar with authentic rosehip seed oil; 3) Are getting good results because its an oil and any natural oil is good for the face. For me, since I'm unsure of what kind of oil I actually got, I won't be using it and have requested a refund (which is currently processing). I've since placed an order with a national, reputable brand of organic, cold-pressed rosehip seed oil, one that has both the distinct color and smell of genuine rosehip seed oil.
